  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_32a3ea9f-e8e6-4f03-801b-9e3edeed7799'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<span id="freeTextContainer18242577122880531559"><i>Daughter of immortals.</i><br/> <br/>Princess Diana longs to prove herself to her legendary warrior sisters.   <span id="freeText18242577122880531559" style="display:none"><i>Daughter of immortals.</i><br /> <br />Princess Diana longs to prove herself to her legendary warrior sisters. But when the opportunity finally comes, she throws away her chance at glory and breaks Amazon law—risking exile—to save a mortal. Diana will soon learn that she has rescued no ordinary girl, and that with this single brave act, she may have doomed the world.<br /><br /><i>Daughter of death.</i><br /> <br />Alia Keralis just wanted to escape her overprotective brother with a semester at sea. She doesn’t know she is being hunted by people who think her very existence could spark a world war. When a bomb detonates aboard her ship, Alia is rescued by a mysterious girl of extraordinary strength and forced to confront a horrible truth: Alia is a Warbringer—a direct descendant of the infamous Helen of Troy, fated to bring about an age of bloodshed and misery.<br /><br /><i>Together.</i><br /> <br />Two girls will face an army of enemies—mortal and divine—determined to either destroy or possess the Warbringer. Tested beyond the bounds of their abilities, Diana and Alia must find a way to unleash hidden strengths and forge an unlikely alliance. Because if they have any hope of saving both their worlds, they will have to stand side by side against the tide of war.</span>

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_32885071').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_32885071').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_32885071').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();

        });

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I relate 100%! I usually steer clear of these kind of novels, even if they are canon. But in this case, I happen to love Leigh Bardugo's work and I've<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I relate 100%! I usually steer clear of these kind of novels, even if they are canon. But in this case, I happen to love Leigh Bardugo's work and I've read her essay on Wonder Woman and what she means to her, and I'm excited to see a true fan and great writer try her hand at this. I think DC chose the authors for this round of canon, YA novels really well! :)<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_1599493170" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1599493170" />
    <a title="Emily May" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may"><img alt="Emily May" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528390751p2/4622890.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1599493170?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily May" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily May" href="/user/show/4622890-emily-may">Emily May</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4622890-emily-may?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1599493170" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6763764638049362116"><blockquote>
  <i>“Sister in battle,” murmured Diana, “I am shield and blade to you.”<br/>“And friend.”<br/>“And always your friend.”</i>
</blockquote><br/>Wonder Woman has gotten quite the makeover this year and I must confess: <b>I really like it</b>. From the movie with Gal Gadot, to this wicked little tale of female empowerment, one of my least favourite superheroes is rapidly becoming a new favourite. And apparently <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29749098.Catwoman__DC_Icons___4_' title='Catwoman (DC Icons, #4) by Sarah J. Maas' rel='nofollow noopener'>Catwoman</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29749094.Superman__DC_Icons___3_' title='Superman (DC Icons, #3) by Matt de la Pena' rel='nofollow noopener'>Superman</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29749090.Batman_Nightwalker__DC_Icons___2_' title='Batman Nightwalker (DC Icons, #2) by Marie Lu' rel='nofollow noopener'>Batman</a> are also being remade by popular YA authors. After this, I'm excited for more.<br/><br/>You know, at first, I</span>
  <span id="freeText6763764638049362116" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“Sister in battle,” murmured Diana, “I am shield and blade to you.”<br />“And friend.”<br />“And always your friend.”</i>
</blockquote><br />Wonder Woman has gotten quite the makeover this year and I must confess: <b>I really like it</b>. From the movie with Gal Gadot, to this wicked little tale of female empowerment, one of my least favourite superheroes is rapidly becoming a new favourite. And apparently <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29749098.Catwoman__DC_Icons___4_" title="Catwoman (DC Icons, #4) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">Catwoman</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29749094.Superman__DC_Icons___3_" title="Superman (DC Icons, #3) by Matt de la Pena" rel="nofollow noopener">Superman</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29749090.Batman_Nightwalker__DC_Icons___2_" title="Batman Nightwalker (DC Icons, #2) by Marie Lu" rel="nofollow noopener">Batman</a> are also being remade by popular YA authors. After this, I'm excited for more.<br /><br />You know, at first, I was a touch disappointed that Bardugo didn't take this opportunity to have a gay romance for Wonder Woman. When she opened Diana's story by swapping out the arrival of army captain, Steve Trevor, for a Greek/African-American girl called Alia, I was secretly shipping them. And yet, I soon realized that Bardugo was doing something just as important-- <b>showing the power of female friendships above all else</b>.<br /><br />I expected certain things from this book - action, death, drama, Greek mythology, a hint of romance - and I definitely got them, but I was surprised by several things. I was surprised by the strength of the characters and their relationships, and how well the author used dialogue to create warm, funny and touching dynamics between them. I was surprised that it was, at times, a funny book. And I was surprised by how much emotion Bardugo packed into it.<br /><br />In this Wonder Woman story, Alia is on board a ship near the island where Diana and her Amazonian sisters live when a bomb detonates. Diana pulls her from the ship, but soon discovers her act of bravery may lead to disaster for both the human world and the Amazons. Alia is a Warbringer, and she unwittingly brings death and war wherever she goes. <br /><br />Determined to save the world and Alia, Diana sets out to find the last resting place of Helen of Troy, and hopefully put an end to Alia's destiny. They move from Themyscira to New York City to Southern Greece, joined by Alia's brother and their friends, Nim and Theo, along the way. <b>Girls sticking up for one another is a major theme, as is friendship in general</b>. <br /><br />It was also very refreshing to see an <b>almost entirely non-white/European cast of central characters</b>. Aside from the white Diana, Alia and her brother are Greek/African-American and identify as black, Theo is Brazilian, and Nim is Indian, gay, fat and so very fucking awesome.<br /><br />What I thought was an interesting choice that somehow worked is that the author kind of makes this Wonder Woman story as much about the other characters as it is about Diana Prince. With superhero stories, I almost always feel like every other character exists in relation to the superhero, revolving around them and having no real individuality. But that's just not the case here. <b>Each character is important and memorable</b>. I cared about Diana Prince in this book, sure, but I cared about the others just as much.<br /><br />The ending closes this chapter but leaves us with the suggestion that there could be more Wonder Woman books in the future. I can only hope there is.<br /><br /><a href="http://thebookgeek.org" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thebookgeekreviews" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thebookgeek01" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://instagram.com/emleemay" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/EmilyMayTheBookGeek" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6763764638049362116" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2205321117" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2205321117" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2205321117?book_show_action=true">Sep 18, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=2018-popsugar-reading-challenge">2018-popsugar-reading-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=us-ya">us-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2205321117" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16551010770683142819">Okay, <b>
  <i>maybe </i>
</b>it's just me...but I was expecting <b>
  <i>more</i>
</b> <br/><br/>Diana, along with everyone she's ever known, lives on a secret island - devoted to the <b>strongest female warriors</b> known to mankind.<blockquote>
  <i>Sisters in battle, I am shield and blade to you. As I breathe, your enemies will know no sanctuary. While I live, your cause is mine.</i>
</blockquote>Every warrior has proven herself time, and time again...<b>well, except for Diana.</b><br/><br/>Diana is the only one who was born (and raised) on the island. And while she's loved by all...</span>
  <span id="freeText16551010770683142819" style="display:none">Okay, <b>
  <i>maybe </i>
</b>it's just me...but I was expecting <b>
  <i>more</i>
</b> <br /><br />Diana, along with everyone she's ever known, lives on a secret island - devoted to the <b>strongest female warriors</b> known to mankind.<blockquote>
  <i>Sisters in battle, I am shield and blade to you. As I breathe, your enemies will know no sanctuary. While I live, your cause is mine.</i>
</blockquote>Every warrior has proven herself time, and time again...<b>well, except for Diana.</b><br /><br />Diana is the only one who was born (and raised) on the island. And while she's loved by all...there are a few that question her presence.<br /><br />When a mysterious, and severely injured, teenager (Alia) washes up on the island, Diana puts all the warriors at risk by allowing her safe haven.<br /><br />Alia is actually<b> a harbinger of war </b>- where ever she goes, whomever she contacts, essentially any and all things connected to her will bring about a war...that is, unless she is <b>murdered</b> before she comes into her full powers.<br /><br />Diana understands this, but she refuses to give in. <b>She finds another way...but it comes at a cost.</b><br /><br /> Will she make it, and prove to her family that she's truly a warrior?<b> Or will she die trying?</b><br /><br />Now, don't get me wrong. <b>The story was nice. <i>And that's about it. </i></b><br /><br />Wonder Woman is so flawless as an adult...and she's just about as flawless as a teen. Sure, she's a little clueless but she's so confident and strong, that it's like a 30-year-old hanging out with the kiddies. <blockquote>
  <i>Because people are always going to look. They’re always going to judge, so you can say nothing or you can at least answer back.</i>
</blockquote>I get that we are seeing Diana as we've never seen her before...but did it have to be such a<b> cookie-cutter story? </b> This book felt too much like <b>a cheesy YA lit novel.</b><blockquote>
  <i>I am done being careful. I am done being quiet. Let them see me angry. Let them hear me wail at the top of my lungs.</i>
</blockquote> However, there was something that did make this one stand out - Leigh Bardugo handled race really well in this novel. <br /><br />I feel like there are so many books that <b>treat race as <i>Race</i></b> - and wrap the entire story around Race. I'm all for having books about Race but sometimes it's really nice to have books with race as a side-part of the story. (Does that make sense?)<br /><br />And I'm eternally grateful that this was one of those. It definitely didn't fall into the typical YA trope of <b>white-on-white</b>.<br /><br />I enjoyed how Leigh Bardugo slips in diversity gently, and matter-of-factly, so that the story always <b>includes race but it's sole purpose isn't to discuss Race. </b><br /><br />I also enjoyed how the side-characters outshone the mains - it's nice to have moments where you become entirely invested in subplots and side relations.<br /><br /><b>Overall - a nice read, but not one that I'll be going back to.</b><blockquote>
  <i>We cannot spend our lives in hiding, wondering what we might accomplish if given the chance. We have to take that chance ourselves.</i>
</blockquote> P.s. Lol, who would've expected so many quotes to be product of a soothsayer and an encouraging-kitten-poster-in-the-guidance-office...<br /><br /><i>The 2018 POPSUGAR Reading Challenge - a book with alliteration in the title</i><br /><br /><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br /><br />Happy Reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16551010770683142819" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1623457578" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1623457578" />
    <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin"><img alt="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603831478p2/17438949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1623457578?book_show_action=true">Jul 14, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin">Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=fantasy-all">fantasy-all</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=own">own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1623457578" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1905084926188023283">One of the shortest reviews to what I thought would be a long review of one of my favorite comic book characters. <br/><br/><img alt=' ' src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1504096275ra/23724596.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Wonder Woman and the Hulk were my favorite characters of all time when I was growing up. I watched and own the shows. I just love them still. Superman followed shortly after and then several more as I got older. Soooooo, I was really disappointed that this book didn't blow me away. I thought it would have all of the stars. I love old school Diana. <br/><br/>All the stars goes to Wonder Woman a</span>
  <span id="freeText1905084926188023283" style="display:none">One of the shortest reviews to what I thought would be a long review of one of my favorite comic book characters. <br><br><img alt=" " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1504096275ra/23724596.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Wonder Woman and the Hulk were my favorite characters of all time when I was growing up. I watched and own the shows. I just love them still. Superman followed shortly after and then several more as I got older. Soooooo, I was really disappointed that this book didn't blow me away. I thought it would have all of the stars. I love old school Diana. <br><br>All the stars goes to Wonder Woman and I liked Alia well enough but it just didn't hit me the right way. I didn't care for anyone else in the book. Don't get me wrong, I love Leigh Bardugo and her Six of Crows duology but I just didn't love this one. <br><br>I don't understand why books have to be changed around to some weird different stuff and I don't even know how to explain what I mean. Lol <br><br>I'm glad so many loved it to death because this is the way of the new world. I'm hoping that someone will write a more adult Wonder Woman book down the road and have it more to the real story line then bending to the world all young adult books are taking. I'm glad that Diana wasn't seen as stupid at least. It wasn't great, it wasn't bad, it was okay. <br><br>Mel ♥</span>
  <a data-text-id="1905084926188023283" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2095806050" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2095806050" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2095806050?book_show_action=true">Aug 17, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=superheroes">superheroes</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2095806050" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer260827806175112649"><i>
  <blockquote>‘‘Sister in battle, I am shield and blade to you. As I breathe, your enemies will know no sanctuary. While I live, your cause is mine.’’</blockquote>
</i><br/>If you’re expecting this to be anything like Leigh Bardugo’s previous written works, expect no more. It would be a bad idea if you did, because this is a very different beast.<br/><br/>Wonder Woman is a legend, but before she became one, she was just a princess, trying to prove to herself and her sisters that she is much, much more than that. That she is a true Amazon</span>
  <span id="freeText260827806175112649" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>‘‘Sister in battle, I am shield and blade to you. As I breathe, your enemies will know no sanctuary. While I live, your cause is mine.’’</blockquote>
</i><br />If you’re expecting this to be anything like Leigh Bardugo’s previous written works, expect no more. It would be a bad idea if you did, because this is a very different beast.<br /><br />Wonder Woman is a legend, but before she became one, she was just a princess, trying to prove to herself and her sisters that she is much, much more than that. That she is a true Amazon.<br /><br />An opportunity presents itself for Diana to challenge herself and explore her greatest strengths, while simultaneously possibly saving the world. So she takes it. <br /><br />Diana is a beautiful, strong woman—young lady, actually—no surprise there. Reading about her life and past and culture lit my brain like a thousand Christmas lights. I only wanted more. Her sisters are worth getting to know also.<br /><br />Which is unfortunate in this case, because we do not get the chance to. They are introduced to the bare minimum and quickly, as most of the novel is spent in company of Diana, Alia and the latter’s entourage. <br /><br />I have nothing bad to say about Alia, but I do find underwhelming that this book was as much about her as it was about Diana. I guess I should have seen it coming, given the fact that the title is <i>Wonder Woman: Warbringer</i>.<br /><br />I thought it would be about Diana first and foremost, but that’s not the case here. Alia’s friends are quirky and lively—except for her rigid brother. They would make wonderful secondary characters in a contemporary novel. But in a fantasy one, they do not fit well.<br /><br />They often have unimportant, silly, childish conversations—banter, basically—even in the midst of danger. Some readers like that, but I don’t. I believe it takes away from the seriousness of the atmosphere. <br /><br />The plot is great, though. The action scenes are exciting and the writing is good. There are even meaningful quotes to ponder. Really, if it wasn’t for Alia and her company, I would have given this book at least four starts, though probably more. Now I hope <i>Catwoman: Soulstealer</i> will be about Catwoman exactly, and not Catwoman and her kitty friends. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="260827806175112649" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1773235906" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1773235906" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1773235906?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780141387369" href="/book/show/35226184-wonder-woman">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2018">read-in-2018</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1773235906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17075333168852778469"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1505783819i/23959360._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I imagine all wars look the same to those who die in them.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>First off, Leigh Bardugo is honestly the queen of writing and I’m not sure what any of us did to deserve her, but I am forever and always going to count her as a blessing. This story is so beautifully written, and I had to tab so many pages with powerful quotes. Leigh also always writes diverse casts that I fall instantly in love with. Like, when do I get a full book about Nim? Because I need that in my life immediately. <br/><br/>➽<b>Di</b></span>
  <span id="freeText17075333168852778469" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1505783819i/23959360._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I imagine all wars look the same to those who die in them.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>First off, Leigh Bardugo is honestly the queen of writing and I’m not sure what any of us did to deserve her, but I am forever and always going to count her as a blessing. This story is so beautifully written, and I had to tab so many pages with powerful quotes. Leigh also always writes diverse casts that I fall instantly in love with. Like, when do I get a full book about Nim? Because I need that in my life immediately. <br><br>➽<b>Diana</b> – White, Wonder Woman herself, obviously a total badass. <br>➽<b>Alia</b> – Black, a Warbringer, a confirmed angel in my eyes, Jason’s sister.<br>➽<b>Jason</b> – Black, Alia’s brother, has helped raise Alia since their parent’s death.<br>➽<b>Nim</b> – Indian, my queer baby, chubby, my sarcastic queen.<br>➽<b>Theo</b> – Brazilian, Jason’s best friend, funny, must be protected at all costs. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1499892188i/23278675._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Beautiful art by <a href="https://www.jenbartel.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Jen Bartel</a>, my celebrity crush. <i>*swoons forever*</i> <br><br>So, this book really starts off with a bang <i>*wink*</i>, when a ship explodes near Themyscira, the island where the Amazons live and there is no fear of war or conflict. But on Themyscira, only strong woman, who have proven themselves during their human life, can reside. Well, except Diana, who has been made her from the ground itself by her mother and the queen of the island. Even though Diana’s mother loves her with all her being, a few of the other women are hesitant to accept her, because they feel she hasn’t “proven herself.” And one of the only rules of Themyscira is that no human is ever allowed to step foot on its shores. <br><br>But Diana witnesses the ship explosion, and finds a lone survivor that she can’t help but rescue and bring back to Themyscira. But the island feels the human’s presence, and starts to attack itself. Diana then seeks out an Oracle who tells her the options she has, and the paths she can take, to save not only her island, but the world itself.<br><br>We are then swept away on a tale that spans from New York City to Greece, from humans to ancient Gods, about powerful girls, unconditional friendships, and the cruelness of men. But the heart of this story is friendship, and how unconditional love from the people you choose to call family is the most powerful force in the world. And the found family in this makes me weep with happiness. I truly love these characters. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Who tells those stories? Tales of vengeful goddesses who wager in human lives for vanity's sake? Of course men believe a woman's power must lie in the fineness of her features, the shapeliness of her limbs. You know better, Daughter of Earth.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>There is also a wonderful discussion about privilege that is brought up throughout this entire book. And how no amount of money will ever be able to alter how people will see your skin color and/or perceive your culture, how no amount of money will never erase oppression, and how discrimination happens in every single economic level in our society, regardless of what people who can’t see passed their white privilege say. I loved this constantly being brought up, and some of these experiences that were talked about are exactly what marginalized teens need to read, and see, and understand that they are perfect the way they are, but our world is just an ugly place that hopefully won’t be so ugly with their generation. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“It's the people who never learn the word impossible who make history, because they're the ones who keep trying.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>I will also continue on with the series with <a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Batman by Marie Lu</a>! But, sadly and ultimately, I just don’t think superhero books are for me. I totally enjoyed reading this, but something just kept me from loving it, so I’m going to blame it on that. I still think this is a very worthwhile and important read, and I’m so happy that I finally was able to get around to it!<br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2952991662" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2952991662" />
    <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale"><img alt="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577855357p2/69106439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2952991662?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥" href="/user/show/69106439-virginia-ronan-herondale">Virginia Ronan ♥ Herondale ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141387376" href="/book/show/34443972-wonder-woman">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2952991662" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5031391965003427604"><i>”As I breathe, your enemies will know no sanctuary. While I live, your cause is mine.”</i><br/><br/>The more I thought about this book, the more I realized that <b>“Wonder Woman”</b> is one of those books you could easily transform into a movie. There were just so many scenes I could picture in a movie and even though this made my entire reading experience very vivid and highly entertaining, it unfortunately also meant that a little bit of my enjoyment went missing. <br/><br/>“Why is that?” you might ask and I’ll try to give </span>
  <span id="freeText5031391965003427604" style="display:none"><i>”As I breathe, your enemies will know no sanctuary. While I live, your cause is mine.”</i><br /><br />The more I thought about this book, the more I realized that <b>“Wonder Woman”</b> is one of those books you could easily transform into a movie. There were just so many scenes I could picture in a movie and even though this made my entire reading experience very vivid and highly entertaining, it unfortunately also meant that a little bit of my enjoyment went missing. <br /><br />“Why is that?” you might ask and I’ll try to give you a proper answer. When I read a book I want my own fantasy to kick in and I don’t only want to imagine those moments but I also want to be surprised. So if I can picture them so easily this ultimately means that I already have a similar scene in my mind and this is never good. *lol* <br /><br />Don’t get me wrong! I really loved this and it was a lot of fun, the “movie factor” was just too strong for my taste though. XD Especially because I recently saw the movie with Gal Gadot and always thought, I really would have loved to see this book as the movie instead of the actual movie. *lol* Because let’s face it: Leigh’s script was way better than the run of the mill Hollywood screenplay. <br />Yes, you read right and I stand by it. ;-P Leigh Bardugo is queen and even one of my four star reviews won’t change that. *lol* <br /><br />On a more personal note: I started this book as a buddy read with my online bestie but about 10% into the book he dropped out of our BR and I had to finish it on my own. It’s sad we couldn’t read the book together but I understand his reasons so yeah, there’s that. &gt;_&lt;<br /><br />And now onwards to one of my more lengthy reviews. ;-)<br /><br /><b>The characters:</b><br /><br /><b>
  <u>Here’s your turning point! Either you move on and leave the safety of Themyscira (what a difficult word!!) or you decide to stay on the island and miss the opportunity to be spoiled! It’s up to you, choose wisely my young warrior! ;-P</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>Alia:</b><br /><br /><i>”Warbringer. Procatalysia. Haptandra. They could call it whatever they wanted. It sounded a lot like monster.”</i><br /><br />Alia… Mhmm what to say about her? I think in this story she kind of represented the typical heroine. I mean she didn’t want to be a Warbringer and she would have rather preferred to die than to be the reason for the 3rd world war. So her character definitely went along with the characteristical attributes of a martyr and she had that sacrificial victim vibe down to a T. *lol* Unfortunately this also meant that we barely got to know her as a person. I mean yes, we get that she was a brainiac and a shy outsider but that’s about it. Which is very sad, because I really would have liked to see all of her different facets and for an MC this just wasn't enough for me. &gt;_&lt;<br /><br /><b>Diana:</b><br /><br /><i>”We cannot spend our lives in hiding, wondering what we might accomplish if given the chance. We have to take that chance ourselves.”</i><br /><br />Come to think of it the same could be said for Diana. She’s one of those super strong and righteous characters that throw around life lessons and quotes like nobody’s business! Haha! I’m not gonna lie, I kinda liked that about her, but it also made her a pretty innocent and bland character to read about. There were no rough edges and I was somehow reminded of Alina in “Shadow and Bone”. I can’t shake the feeling that Diana would have turned out to be a really great character if she would have been given a chance to thrive in a sequel. *lol* As far as I know there doesn’t exist a second book though, so I suppose I’ll just have to accept the fact that her character won’t be fleshed out and that this is everything we'll ever get. XD *sniff* There would have been so much potential...<br /><br /><i>”We can’t help the way we’re born. We can’t help what we are, only what life we choose to make for ourselves.”</i> <br /><br /><b>Nim:</b><br /><br /><i>”For all my big talk, I’ve never brought a girl home. I’ve never even hinted at that stuff to my parents. I’m afraid if I do, it will all fall apart.”</i><br /><br />Boy, could I relate to Nim!!! I loved this girl so much and considering that she was just a side character, she and Theo actually saved the book for me. It’s kind of interesting how the side characters got a chance to shine in “Wonder Woman” and how I ended up thinking that the MCs were nothing special. *lol* But here it is and I accept it. XD Whilst I missed the depth in Diana’s and Alia’s character I got plenty of that with Nim. ;-) She was an amazing sidekick and her comments were priceless! XD You might call it the “Nikolai Lantsov” effect and Nim as well as Theo had plenty of it. *lol*I loved how fierce and independent Nim was and even though she stood on her own feet and was able to defend herself she still had a vulnerable and insecure side that was revealed throughout the course of the book. I really would have loved to read even more about her but unfortunately my wish wasn’t granted, which made me very sad because the world needs more Nim's for sure! T_T<br /><br /><i>”What’s a supermodel?” Diana asked.<br />Nim stared at her.<br />“Uh, Diana’s homeschooled,” said Alia.<br />“Under a rock?” asked Nim.</i><br /><br /><i>”Because the whole world loves to tell us what we can’t do, that we aren’t good enough. The people in your own house should be on your side. It’s the people who never learn the word impossible who make history, because they’re the ones who keep trying.”</i><br /><br /><i>”Maybe it feels easier that way, just being invisible instead of always worrying what people think of you.”<br />Nim’s voice was surprisingly emphatic. “But that’s a choice, too, right? Because people are always going to look. They’re always going to judge, so you can say nothing or you can at least answer back.”</i><br /><br /><b>Jason:</b><br /><br /><i>”Is that stupid?” he asked. It was the first time she’d seen him look anything less than sure of himself. “To want a chance at greatness?”</i><br /><br />Urgh! Jason! You can bet your lovely behind on the fact that I knew he was one of the bad guys the very moment he opened his mouth for the first time. *lol* I wasn’t fooled by him… not even for a second. XD He made a very bad villain though because his motives were really stupid. I mean yes, he wanted to get a chance to shine. So what? You’re going to risk your life in a war that will drag the entire world into mayhem just to get a shot at greatness? Who’s going to remember you when the entire world is descending into chaos? I think there are enough wars already and humanity is doing a great job at killing itself without the additional help of a Warbringer. At some point of the book Alia and Diana tried to tell him too, but of course he didn’t listen. XD Well, in the end he got what he deserved and even though the way it was executed made my eyes roll and sort of reminded me of the ending of “Indiana Jones and the Last Crusade” (except of the getting old and crumbling to dust part) it was still kind of fitting for him. *lol*<br /><br /><i>”Humans can’t hold to peace, Diana,” Jason said. His gaze was steady, certain, and in his words she heard the echo of her mother’s voice. “We’re brutes and have been since our beginning. If we can’t have peace, then at least give us a chance at a beautiful death.”</i> <br /><br /><b>Theo:</b><br /><br /><i>”You mean we’re all going to join hands and sing folk songs?”<br />“That sounds unpleasant,” said Diana.<br />“Come on!” said Theo. “Peace, love, the Age of Asparagus.”<br />“Aquarius,” corrected Nim.</i><br /><br />*LOL* Theo, this brilliant little piece of sh**! Haha! I can’t say how much I adored him. Yes, he was a nerd but he was a sexy nerd and I could totally understand that Alia had the hots for him. XD I completely fell in love with him and his pointy shoes as well. *lol* ;-P He provided the easy banter and the funny moments of this story and I can’t understand why Jason wanted to kill him! I mean he was his best friend, he stood by him and even though everyone suspected him of being the villain he took it in stride and proved them wrong! He could have been offended by them suspecting him but instead he tried to understand them and overcame his hurt. =) Plus even though he might have been a skinny son of a gun he had his heart at the right place and managed to be cool when you least expected it. ;-) So yes, I’m a Theo fan now! XD<br /><br /><i>”Diana,” said Nim. “Kick Jason’s ass.”<br />She frowned, confused. “Specifically his ass?”<br />“Yeah.”<br />“Why?”<br />Without looking up from the keys, Theo said, “New York tradition.”</i><br /><br /><b>The relationships &amp; ships:</b><br /><br /><u>Alia &amp; Diana:</u><br /><br /><i>”You are being hunted.”<br />“Hunted,” Alia said flatly. “For my silky pelt?”<br />“Because you are haptandra.”<br />“Say again?”<br />“A Warbringer.”<br />“I’m not into gaming.”</i><br /><br />Haha! The dialogues between those two! &lt;3 They sure as hell made an interesting team, yet they still worked out somehow. *lol* I really liked their strong bond and friendship and I wish they would have gotten a chance to spend more time with each other. After everything that happened the ending felt rather rushed and when I closed the final page of the book I couldn’t help but wish for a little bit more time with those two. I didn’t like that Diana had to go back to her island immediately and to me it felt like they didn’t get a decent chance at closure. I mean Diana would have deserved to be with them, even if it would have been for just a little while. &gt;_&lt;<br /><br /><u>Alia &amp; Theo:</u><br /><br /><i>”I drove,” said Theo. “Once.”<br />“That was a golf cart,” said Alia.<br />“So? It had four wheels and went vroom.”<br />“You crashed it into a tree.”<br />“I’ll have you know that tree had been drinking.”</i><br /><br />Ahhh I loved how well they knew each other and yet they still never went for a romance. *lol* I guess they both might have waited for the right time and as it seems it finally arrived. Thank the gods! Because those two fit together perfectly! XD I knew they’d be awesome the moment Theo was introduced and I longed to read about their first kiss! Which didn’t happen!!! Like <b>OMG!!! WHY LEIGH??!!!!</b> A little kiss never hurt nobody! &gt;_&lt; Guess I’ll just have to picture their happily ever after in my mind. *sighs*<br /><br /><i>”The night of the party at the Met, how come you complimented everyone but me?”<br />He grinned. “Because you in that gold dress turned my brain to mush.”<br />She rolled her eyes. “Right.”<br />He took a couple of steps, then paused. “Alia?” he called back. <br />“What, Theo?”<br />“That night, at the party? You looked like buried treasure.”</i><br /><br /><u>Diana &amp; Jason:</u><br /><br /><i>”You’re pretty enough, Jason Keralis. But hardly intimidating.”<br />His eyelids stuttered. “Pretty?”</i><br /><br />Pff, I didn’t get to witness my Aleo ship but unfortunately I had to watch the shipwreck of Dison! *lol* This relationship was doomed right from the beginning because I didn’t feel any chemistry between those two! They danced, they laughed, hell, they even spent a night together yet they didn’t even evoke a shred of emotion in me. &gt;_&lt; I guess their impeccable behaviour made it kind of hard to enjoy their relationship. They were both too bland to make a decent couple and I could only roll my eyes whenever they were supposed to have a romantic moment. *sighs deeply* Nope, those two just didn’t work for me. #SorryNotSorry <br /><br /><i>”I think you’ve grown too used to people saying yes to you.”<br />“Have I?”<br />“But you have no idea how much I enjoy saying no.”</i><br /><br /><u>Nim &amp; Theo:</u><br /><br /><i>”Nim, you look like a delicious confection, a walking, talking – probably poisonous – petit four.”<br />“In that case,” said Nim, “bite me.”</i><br /><br />Now that’s what I call a perfect frenemy relationship. Haha! I wonder if it was just Alia’s Warbringer influence or if they kept up their banter after the happenings at the spring. *lol* I like to believe that they started to like each other and developed some sort of love-hate sibling friendship over the years. XD In the book they were like cat and mouse and their entertainment effect was very high. If it would have been up to me there would have been even more crazy conversations between them but I guess it was perfect the way Leigh decided to handle it. ;-)<br /><br /><i>”We’re the villains! It’s always cooler to be the villain. You get to wear black and have a lair and brood. Besides, girls can’t resist a bad boy.”<br />“You are such an idiot,” said Nim.<br />He tapped his temple. “It’s not my fault you lack the vision.”</i><br /><br /><b>Conclusion:</b><br /><br /><b>“Wonder Woman – Warbringer”</b> was a highly entertaining book that reminded me a lot of all those modern blockbusters you can watch at the movies. There was plenty of easy banter and a great and diverse cast of MCs and side-characters alike. I loved that a lot of myths and legends weren’t only mentioned but also woven into the story and if there was one thing I didn’t like, then it was the fact that the MCs didn’t really convince me. In my opinion the side characters were more intriguing than the MCs and this in combination with the rather abrupt ending ultimately caused me to rate this book with only four stars. If you’re looking for an easy and funny read this definitely should be able to satisfy your hunger though. ;-)<br />_____________________________<br /><br />I recently saw the movie and I already knew about the “DC Icons” series when I happened to find this at one of my libraries. =) <br />Leigh Bardugo writing the story of Wonder Woman? Count me in! XD<br /><br />I’m a huge fan of “Batman”, “Catwoman” and “Superman” as well so let’s hope that my library has the rest of the series too. *fingers crossed*<br /><br /><b>AND</b> <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/99779228-craig" rel="nofollow noopener">Mr. Babygreys</a> , I know you’re reading this so would you be so kind and go for another buddy read with me? It would be such a pleasure! ;-P *princely bow* There I asked you really nicely! This gotta count for something, right? XD<br /><br />P.S: <s>If not I’ll ignore all my princely manners and pull your ear instead.</s> *lol*</span>
  <a data-text-id="5031391965003427604" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2249260935" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2249260935" />
    <a title="Khurram" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25493797-khurram"><img alt="Khurram" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1383996638p2/25493797.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2249260935?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khurram" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khurram" href="/user/show/25493797-khurram">Khurram</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141387376" href="/book/show/34443972-wonder-woman">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2249260935" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14165536227912008377">An ok to good book. I would have liked to give it 3.5 stars. There are parts of the book that are really good but on the whole the book is very slow. I think part of what I had to overcome in this story, was forgetting everything I already knew about Wonder Woman. I think Leigh Bardugo did a great job of Diane, but not quite as great on Wonder Woman. However this is not a bad thing as in this story, Diane is quite a bit younger then previous incarnations of her have been, and has all the inexper</span>
  <span id="freeText14165536227912008377" style="display:none">An ok to good book. I would have liked to give it 3.5 stars. There are parts of the book that are really good but on the whole the book is very slow. I think part of what I had to overcome in this story, was forgetting everything I already knew about Wonder Woman. I think Leigh Bardugo did a great job of Diane, but not quite as great on Wonder Woman. However this is not a bad thing as in this story, Diane is quite a bit younger then previous incarnations of her have been, and has all the inexperience and insecurities of growing up. Therefore she should not by the warrior she is to become yet.<br /><br />This is a complete remake of the origin story. It is set in the modern world not in World War 2 time. One subtle point I really liked was when Diane and the Amazon’s talk about “man’s world” they don’t just mean men but mortals in general. I liked all the side characters in the book, I think they were written really well except when the Greek “Gods” appeared. I know Wonder Woman’s history is based on Greek mythology, and if they were just mentioned that was fine, but a couple of times they appeared I still do not understand why, and the other I think the story would have been better for Diane to triumph or fail on her own. I would have also liked more fight in the story considering her warrior heritage. Though I did like the final fight, the the one before that sucked.<br /><br />All in all a good take new take on Diane. I would not mind a continuation of this incarnation of Diane to returns as the true warrior/Wonder Woman, I think there is enough left to warrant that.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14165536227912008377" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1597053029" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1597053029" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1597053029?book_show_action=true">Aug 30, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=superheroes">superheroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=retelling">retelling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=magical-fantasy">magical-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1597053029" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6455292715421418741"><b>Okay so this was a definite pocketful of feministic glory.</b> I confess I was worried! As much as I <i>adore</i> Leigh Bardugo, I actually hadn't (UNTIL NOW) read a superhero-adaption-novel that didn't make me feel like swallowing rusty sporks. But this reads fully like a decent superpowered exciting action adventure story <b>and I thoroughly loved it!</b> Even though I will confess it was rather slow. And who the heck knows what's going on with my paperback, but the font was <i>so tiny</i> I lost about 9 years off my </span>
  <span id="freeText6455292715421418741" style="display:none"><b>Okay so this was a definite pocketful of feministic glory.</b> I confess I was worried! As much as I <i>adore</i> Leigh Bardugo, I actually hadn't (UNTIL NOW) read a superhero-adaption-novel that didn't make me feel like swallowing rusty sporks. But this reads fully like a decent superpowered exciting action adventure story <b>and I thoroughly loved it!</b> Even though I will confess it was rather slow. And who the heck knows what's going on with my paperback, but the font was <i>so tiny</i> I lost about 9 years off my eyeballs.<br /><br />But 10/10 am willing to suffer for Diana.<br /><br /><b>ALSO NOTE:</b> I actually knew NOTHING about Wonder Woman, apart from the duh obvious <i>she's Wonder Woman</i> before reading this. I haven't seen the latest DC film and I've read like maybe one comic??? I think??? <b>So you can fully read and enjoy this without being a WW nerd.</b> Just be a nerd though. Always be a nerd if you can.<br /><br /><br /><b> L I K E S:</b><br /><b> • Okay but do you know what I'm freaking out over? IT FEATURES STRONG FEMALE FRIENDSHIPS!!!!!</b> I shouldn't have to be this excited BUT I AM. Because holy heck, I can't even remember the last time I read a good solid female friendship in YA that didn't dissolve into jealousy or cattiness over a boy. But WW gives us not one but TWO solidly epic, uplifting and empowering female friendships. I adored Alia and Diana's bond. They were sisters of war by the end, even if Alia was a smol breakable human nerd and Diana is like AMAZON EPIC. I'm so so impressed.<br />•<b> Feminism FTW.</b> All the feminism. You will only see women empowered here. I think I have an emotion over this omg.<br />• <b> I also adored all the mythology of course!</b> I didn't realise how steeped in Greek mythology this would be, sot hat was a pleasant surprise. <b>Think Percy Jackson = but with epic girls.</b><br />• <b>It's also super diverse, with like ALL the characters being POC!</b> Like how awesome is that?! Here is an action adventure story featuring POC in all the leading roles. (Except for Diana I <i>think</i>? But I'm not sure what her skin colour was. I was imagining her kind of Mediterranean complexion but she was made out of CLAY so like hello.)<br />•<b> It was so so funny!</b> The dialogue and banter was like LAUGH OUT LOUD WORTHY!!!<br />• <b>It also has quite a bit cast, but everyone was so developed and complex.</b> I mean Bardugo is the queen of epic casts and making characters so layered so fast.<br />•<b> I MEAN, JUST SO MUCH CHARACTER APPRECIATION.</b> Diana and Alia take turns narrating, and then there's Alia's BFF, Nim, who is a designer and bi and entirely small and feisty. Then there's Theo who is like a gangly dork and super vain and hilarious and everyone kind of wants to kill him. #Nice. Also of course Jason, Alia's older brother, who is Mister Bossy Pants but loves his sister so much and just wants her safe. EPIC CAST IS EPIC.<br />• <b>Diana experiencing the mortal world was HILARIOUS.</b> That will never get old omg I laughed so much.<br />•<b> There is very very little romance!</b> I mean there's a bit, but like yay!<br />• <b>Also it would make a freaking fantastic movie.</b> Just sayin'.<br />• <b>Also shoutout to that line where Diana is called a "magnificent tree".</b> I appreciate all the small humans in this book continually asking her why she is as tall as a mountain.<br /><br /><br /><b>D I S L I K E S:</b><br />•<b> okay, I hate to say it, but it was slow.</b> It took me like forever to read and I frequently felt the plot was predictable. And then one twist in particular (<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Jason turning out to be EVIL MAN <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>) didn't feel built up enough? So YAY for curve balls. But I wanted more grounding for them.<br />•<b> Also Diana was GREAT and I loved her, but she was So Pure So Perfect™ I struggled to be invested.</b> I just connected to Alia way more. I enjoy heroes but also??? I prefer??? The dark side??? Excuse me???<br />• <b>I didn't quite understand why they were working their butts off to save Alia's life, but like....other people died in the crossfire.</b> Ya know, just the nameless blokes. But I NEVER UNDERSTAND THIS TROPE. How come one life is worth more than another? I get that they were trying to "break" the Warbringer curse but stilllllll. Diana's immediately 100% commitment to keep Alia safe just doesn't click with my brain. I think this is because I'm a coldhearted Slytherin so pls don't mind me.<br /><br /><br /><b>ALL IN ALL: Look it was <i>wonderful</i> (HAR HAR I COULDN'T RESIST) and empowering and so delightfully feminist.</b> Maybe it didn't shock me and maaaaybe I wish it'd been faster paced because a whole lotta scenes felt a little like having a corn chip without guacamole, but <b>it was really fun and the writing was A+ and the banter amazing.</b> AM A FAN HERE.<br /><br />(Also can we agree that Theo is Jesper Freaking Fahey? Because he is. 10000%.)<br /><br /><br /><blockquote>"Sure we do," said Theo, swatting at a branch. "We get to the spring, Alia gets cured. We argue over the best choice for our We Saved The World victory dance."<br />"I do enjoy your optimism," said Diana.<br />"And I admire your ability to lift a car over your head without breaking a sweat and look fine as hell doing it," said Theo with a bow.</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"It was woven by Athena on a spindle forged in Hestia's fire, of fibre harvested from Gaia's first tree."<br />"Big deal," said Theo. "You can probably get one on eBay."</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote> "You cannot make this kind of decision," he said. "Go off with someone you barely know. You're <i>seventeen</i>."<br />"And you're the guy who got drunk on eggnog last Christmas and danced to 'Turn The Beat Around' in Aunt Rachel's wig, so stop acting like you're in charge."<br />"We agreed not to mention that ever again," Jason whispered furiously.</blockquote><br /><br /><blockquote>"Because the whole world loves to tell us what we can't do, that we aren't good enough. The people in your own house should be on your side. It's the people who never learn the word <i>impossible</i> who make history, becuase they're the ones who keep trying."</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="6455292715421418741" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer2464019992991693781">Wonder Woman can crush me between her thighs and I'd probably be all heart eyes while she does it. 🤷 ¯\_(ツ)_/¯<br/><br/>i don't think you guys understand how badly i want to live on the island of Themyscira!!! where everything is pure and magical with beautiful, bad ass ladies around every corner!!! <br/><br/>anyways, this book is about Wonder Women aka Diana who was made of clay and bought to life by the gods themselves. on an island where every Amazon has proved themselves worthy to live on in peace, Diana feels </span>
  <span id="freeText2464019992991693781" style="display:none">Wonder Woman can crush me between her thighs and I'd probably be all heart eyes while she does it. 🤷 ¯\_(ツ)_/¯<br /><br />i don't think you guys understand how badly i want to live on the island of Themyscira!!! where everything is pure and magical with beautiful, bad ass ladies around every corner!!! <br /><br />anyways, this book is about Wonder Women aka Diana who was made of clay and bought to life by the gods themselves. on an island where every Amazon has proved themselves worthy to live on in peace, Diana feels unworthy and has to prove that she <i>is</i> a worthy warrior. during one of their races, Diana is determined to shut them up for good and show what she's made of!!! but she gets distracted by a human dying and instead of continuing on with the race, she saves a mortal which is very ""illegal"" and can result in exile. <br /><br />the mortal she saves is Alia, a Warbringer, whose very existence is a magnet for war and fights. but tbh, Alia is a total sweetheart and honestly you won't even be able to bring yourself to hurt a hair on her head, she's so pure!!! the people who want to kill her can choke lnjlsdvsdfkjefj.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>characters!!!</b>
</blockquote><br />→Diana is such a pure, innocent and strong character, i love her so fucking much y'all akbjkvbds. she beats down sexist and gross men, can jump onto airplanes hundreds of feet in the air, while being such an ignorant dork akhcdf. she genuinely made me Laugh Out Loud.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>"What's a supermodel?"<br />"What makes these models super?" inquired Diana, still curious. "Do they have powers?"</b>
</blockquote><br /><br />despite the fact that she can easily crush us with her bare hands, she's so kind and has infinite love for mortals, y'all what did we ever do to deserve her? <br /><br />→Alia is half greek/half black and the purestTM and softestTM person. thinking about Alia's character is like hugging a really soft dog 😍. just because people want to kill each other while they're around her, doesn't mean Alia is a horrible person. it's not her fault she's a magnet for bloodshed and war!!! she just wants to pursue her dreams and live her life without her overprotective brother in every step of her way. she's also so kind, lovely, supporting and loving towards her friends. <br /><br />→Nim is a chubby, queer and Indian cinnamon roll who i'd die for in a heartbeat. she's the type of person who pushes you to do your best and would always be there for you no matter what, and she's also so funny??? askflsknvI JUST LOVE HER SO MUCH??? THANKS.<br /><br />→Theo is one of Alia's friends, also a POC (I think he's black). he loves playing video games and is a computer genius. don't mess with him,he can easily hack into all your social media and easily ruin your life (though i doubt he'll do that because he's too good of a person.) he's constantly frowned by his father because he's "not doing anything with his life/wasting his life playing video games instead of pursuing a career" and that shit sucks. he doesn't deserve that shit 😤😤. <br /><br />and can we talk about how he got so excited to be the villains and almost dying? me.<br /><br /><b>ALIAxTHEO</b><br />these two are SO FUCKIGN CUTE SLFKJDBVFAL;KNQBDSBNSDKLGBSO and shy around each other, MY HEART.<br /><br />Diana, Nim and Alia also have such a healthy friendship. there is no girl hate in this house, bitchez. they always push each other to do their best, ALWAYS support each other and they got each others backs!!! you know, the best type of friends are the ones who you can call your family. and this whole squad is a family. i love them.<br /><br />these characters go through so much shit that only makes them grow into better people. it's some very good character development. <br /><br />my only complaints with this book (because HA Sana always has problems with everything) is that it was wayyy too slow. there's a lot of plot build up and the exciting things happen towards the end of the novel. it also read a lotttt like middle grade for me?? and i'm not a big fan of middle grade!!<br /><br />i was hoping to read more about the island and the Amazons, but sadly, there wasn't much of that.<br /><br />ALSO, THAT PLOT TWIST HAD ME SO FUCKING SHOOK, i'm still recovering!!!!!!!!<br /><br />overall, this is one heck of a book and you should read it.<br /><br />----<br />i had to watch the movie Wonder Woman before reading this one and let me tell you that i'm so excited for my eyes to lick every word in this book!!!!!! (and definitely for Batman 😍)</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1793942433" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer3134528641479936966"><i>“You dance differently when you know you won't live forever.”</i><br/><br/>I have seen the film. And this book is better. Fight me.<br/><br/>Full disclosure: I do not care for DC or Marvel. I mean, how many times can an apocalypse be prevented in the last nanosecond until it becomes unrealistic? Until it becomes a cliché? They tell the same story again and again and I am over it. I also do not care for the majority of actors and actresses the companies have hired. I either dislike them or find them boring. Or hate them</span>
  <span id="freeText3134528641479936966" style="display:none"><i>“You dance differently when you know you won't live forever.”</i><br><br>I have seen the film. And this book is better. Fight me.<br><br>Full disclosure: I do not care for DC or Marvel. I mean, how many times can an apocalypse be prevented in the last nanosecond until it becomes unrealistic? Until it becomes a cliché? They tell the same story again and again and I am over it. I also do not care for the majority of actors and actresses the companies have hired. I either dislike them or find them boring. Or hate them because I find them boring. That being said, I do care deeply for Diana Prince. She is a cute little nugget and does not need to be protected because she can defend herself perfectly fine.<br><br>This book was perfect. Not that I expected anything else from Leigh. It was action-packed, it was diverse, it was unexpected. I enjoyed the connection to Greek mythology and have always found it fascinating. It was also super funny. Diana has never seen the world outside her sheltered home before, which is why her reactions are often stunning and hilarious. I also know for a fact the Leigh giggled to herself when she wrote this particular scene:<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1534000172i/26111122.jpg" width="500" height="525" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>One has to love the world wide web.<br><br>Anyway, it was an amazing book and I would love to see a sequel or two in the future. There is lots of potential and a few loose ends that could be picked up on. <br><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/fantasticbooksandwheretofindem/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>

<div id="review_2042794485" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2042794485" />
    <a title="Nina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44463467-nina"><img alt="Nina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597502267p2/44463467.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2042794485?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nina" href="/user/show/44463467-nina">Nina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Library Binding 9780399549748" href="/book/show/32336277-wonder-woman">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">EVERYONE</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44463467-nina?shelf=best-of-the-best">best-of-the-best</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44463467-nina?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2042794485" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2363545869402126961"><i>“I am done being careful. I am done being quiet. Let them see me angry. Let them hear me wail at the top of my lungs.” </i><br/><br/>I’m sitting here right now, trying to write a review for this book and I literally just can’t think of a fitting first sentence because I’m still so overwhelmed by how amazing this book was. ‘Wonder Woman: Warbringer’ is one of the books you pretty much fly through, that absolutely absorbs you right from the beginning and then leaves you sitting there at the end of it, staring a</span>
  <span id="freeText2363545869402126961" style="display:none"><i>“I am done being careful. I am done being quiet. Let them see me angry. Let them hear me wail at the top of my lungs.” </i><br /><br />I’m sitting here right now, trying to write a review for this book and I literally just can’t think of a fitting first sentence because I’m still so overwhelmed by how amazing this book was. ‘Wonder Woman: Warbringer’ is one of the books you pretty much fly through, that absolutely absorbs you right from the beginning and then leaves you sitting there at the end of it, staring at the last page because you can’t believe that it’s already over. It’s definitely one of the best books I’ve read this year so far and my high expectations for it were definitely not disappointed. <br /><br />‘Wonder Woman: Warbringer’ is a very gripping read and there wasn’t a single scene in this novel that bored me. It was full of plot twists that absolutely took me by surprise and left me sitting there with my mouth agape. The book was also very well written though that shouldn’t surprise anyone who’s read at least one of Leigh Bardugo’s novels prior to picking up this little masterpiece. <br /><br />I absolutely adore her writing style and she’s slowly but surely becoming one of my all-time favorite authors. She’s just amazing at writing fighting scenes that are realistic and varied so that you won’t feel like you’re reading the same thing over and over again even if there are several action-packed scenes in her books. Another thing she’s really good at is slipping in funny moments when you don’t expect anything like that to happen and my book is once again full of green sticky notes that I use to highlight funny things.<br /><br />But one of the best things about ‘Wonder Woman: Warbringer’ were definitely the amazing characters Leigh Bardugo has created. Especially, the strong female characters were amazing and kicked butt which I absolutely loved.<br /><br />All in all, ‘Wonder Woman: Warbringer’ is a book that definitely deserves 5 out of 5 stars. I absolutely loved it and I’m probably going to guard it like gold. It’s a novel I would recommend to pretty much everyone and I absolutely can’t wait for Marie Lu’s book because I just love the idea of this entire series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2363545869402126961" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
