    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1974724442" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1974724442" />
    <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries"><img alt="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557144778p2/15335689.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1974724442?book_show_action=true">Jan 02, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" class="user" itemprop="url" name="destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]" href="/user/show/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries">destiny ♡⚔♡ [howling libraries]</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=diverse-reads">diverse-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15335689-destiny-howling-libraries?shelf=owned-physical">owned-physical</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1974724442" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10586004691669234883"><blockquote>
  <i>“We can’t help the way we’re born. We can’t help what we are, only what life we choose to make for ourselves.”</i>
</blockquote><br/>I’ve never been a Wonder Woman fan in my past (I was always more of a Batman type), so I wasn’t sure what to expect going into this book, or whether or not I would enjoy it very much, but it came highly recommended by one of my best friends, and it’s Leigh Bardugo, which meant, if nothing else, I knew I’d like the writing in it. The beginning started off rather slow for me and I felt</span>
  <span id="freeText10586004691669234883" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“We can’t help the way we’re born. We can’t help what we are, only what life we choose to make for ourselves.”</i>
</blockquote><br />I’ve never been a Wonder Woman fan in my past (I was always more of a Batman type), so I wasn’t sure what to expect going into this book, or whether or not I would enjoy it very much, but it came highly recommended by one of my best friends, and it’s Leigh Bardugo, which meant, if nothing else, I knew I’d like the writing in it. The beginning started off rather slow for me and I felt like I was trudging through the first 80-100 pages, which is why this was a 4-star read instead of 5. That said, the entire second half or so of this book was so much fun, and the ending won me over to Diana so much that now I feel like I urgently need a sequel to her story.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i> Amazon. Born of war, destined to be ruled by no one but herself.</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>→ Diana ←</b><br />Diana and I got off to a rocky start, honestly. In the first few chapters, she was such an inherently <i>good</i> person that she fell victim to the “so good they’re boring” trope, and I was starting to wonder what her appeal was. Thankfully, once they left Themyscira, Diana really came into her own as this unbelievably fiery, passionate, badass warrior, and I adored her from that moment on.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i> Their lives were violent, precarious, fragile, but they fought for them anyway, and held to the hope that their brief stay on this earth might count for something.</i>
</blockquote><br />Despite being an immortal, Diana cares so strongly for the humans that she makes incredible sacrifices to help them along the way. I loved her protective nature and the ends she was willing to go to. Not only that, but her entire thought process and narrative throughout the story is just so enjoyable to read; you get such an inside view of her motivations, how pure her intentions are, and how much she wants to make the world a better place.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“I’m a daughter of Nemesis,” she said, “the goddess of divine retribution. You may want to think about how well I can hold a grudge.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>→ Alia ←</b><br />Alia, on the other hand, I loved from the beginning. She is sassy and incredibly bright, and the humor in her narrative is fantastic and genuine. She feels like a real person I could (and would) be friends with, despite being a Warbringer, and Leigh portrays her emotions beautifully: when Alia was proud, I was proud with her. When her heart ached, mine did, too. Through it all, I adored the fact that, despite being the mortal of the pair, she manages to somehow hold her own just as well as Diana does, in her own ways, and it never felt like she was being put in Diana’s shadow.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i> “Sister in battle, I am shield and blade to you. As I breathe, your enemies will know no sanctuary. While I live, your cause is mine.”</i>
</blockquote><br />My favorite thing about both of these young women, though, is how much they grow to love one another. I adored their friendship so much, whether it was in their banter, or their promises to one another, or how passionately they both wanted to help the other succeed in their common goal. I know this book is <i>about</i> Wonder Woman, but really, it’s about Alia, just as much.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i> She’d chosen her soldiers. It was time to go to war.</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>→ war ←</b><br />Much like I would expect from a book about a superhero, this is, more than anything, an action book. While books with a lot of action aren’t always my cup of tea (as we all know, I’m a bigger fan of world- and character-building), <i>WW:W</i> reminded me that Leigh writes battle scenes <i>beautifully.</i> Many authors say that writing a fight scene is one of the toughest things to do well, and I would believe it, because I rarely see them executed as flawlessly as Leigh’s. These scenes are fluid, easy to follow, and descriptive enough that I found myself feeling like I was watching them all play out right before my eyes.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i> A different kind of knight, one who’d chosen to protect the girl the world wanted to destroy; one born to slay dragons, but maybe to befriend them, too.</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>→ mythology ←</b><br />Of course, this story isn’t <i>all</i> action – there’s a tremendous amount of lore and mythology woven into the story and the characters, especially when nearing the end of the book. I don’t remember all the details, but as a child, I used to love staying up long past my bedtime, poring through my aunt’s illustrated mythology books, reading the stories over and over again. Seeing the cameos of so many of those classic beings, and being reminded of their origin stories, was such a wonderful experience that I didn’t expect to be granted so much of in this book, and it made me love Leigh even more for taking the time to be so inclusive.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i> When had she stopped being a child? The first time a guy had whistled at her out of a car window when she was walking to school?</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>→ representation &amp; feminism ←</b><br />Finally, more than anything else in this story, I <i>loved</i> how feminist its values were, and how inclusive the cast was. We had Diana’s stories of how the Amazon women ranged from heterosexual, to bisexual, to lesbian, to asexual, and anything in between. We had Alia’s best friend, Nim, who was the perfect little Indian, plus-size bi girl (and who I loved to bits). There’s Alia and her brother, these beautiful biracial black/Greek siblings, and their friend Theo, a Brazilian teen who’s downright hysterical (if not slightly obnoxious at times). It felt like this book was positively teeming with normalized diversity and feminism, and I loved that so, so much. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>“If you cannot bear our pain, you are not fit to carry our strength.”</i>
</blockquote><br /><b>→ final thoughts ←</b><br />All in all, this book wasn’t perfect for me – it had some pacing issues and a slow start, which is why I dropped it down to 4 stars. That said, it was still vastly enjoyable and I would recommend it if you like fantasy novels with a lot of action elements, or if you’re a mythology geek, or if you just like superheroes and/or Leigh Bardugo’s impeccable writing style.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10586004691669234883" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1941176830" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11180664184482958460">You weren't expecting a rating below 5 stars, were you? xD<br/><br/><a href='http://bit.ly/2pei1LY' rel='nofollow noopener'>Read my full review of <b>Wonder Woman: </b><i>Warbringer</i>!</a><br/><br/>Holy crap on a cracker, <b>this book was freaking amazing! I am utterly speechless, floored, stupefied, and every other possible synonymous adjective.</b> But am I surprised to be feeling this way after finishing this book? Of course not! I'm talking about Leigh freaking Bardugo here. My idol, my inspiration, and in my humble (and totally unbiased) opinion—the most awe-inspiring and talented author</span>
  <span id="freeText11180664184482958460" style="display:none">You weren't expecting a rating below 5 stars, were you? xD<br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/2pei1LY" rel="nofollow noopener">Read my full review of <b>Wonder Woman: </b><i>Warbringer</i>!</a><br><br>Holy crap on a cracker, <b>this book was freaking amazing! I am utterly speechless, floored, stupefied, and every other possible synonymous adjective.</b> But am I surprised to be feeling this way after finishing this book? Of course not! I'm talking about Leigh freaking Bardugo here. My idol, my inspiration, and in my humble (and totally unbiased) opinion—the most awe-inspiring and talented author of our time.<br><br>I also should mention that I have been a long-time Batman fan (so of course, I'm dying for Marie Lu's installment in this series), but . . . I never got into Wonder Woman. Then this book happened. <b>Bardugo truly brings the fierce Amazon to life, and not only that! She also empowers the other female characters by highlighting all of their different forms of strength</b> that they possess, while also emphasizing that none of those strengths are any less valuable or important than the brute physical strength Diana was born with. As a whole, Wonder Woman: Warbringer is <b>a lesson in feminism, sisterhood, love, loss, and holy hell—it's a damn masterpiece.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491681559ra/22436257.gif" width="400" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I will never be skilled enough to find the adequate words to describe what Bardugo's writing does to my soul, though I will keep endeavoring to try. However to Leigh herself, I can only say <i>thank you</i>. You continue to raise the bar higher and higher, and it's truly special.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1491681559ra/22436258.gif" width="400" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Honestly, there is no other author that can move me the way Leigh does. She absolutely never ceases to impress. Definitely as soon as you are able—but especially if you are a Wonder Woman fan—you must get your hands on this outstanding book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11180664184482958460" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2026880377" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer950552607947905086"><b>DNF @ 280 <br/><s>REVIEW TO COME TOMORROW.</s></b><br/><br/><b> THE REVIEW IS POSTED </b> <br/><br/><b>
  <blockquote>
    <pre><br/>She would not fail. And she would not <br/>let fear choose her path.<br/></pre>
  </blockquote>
</b><br/><br/><b>me : if this is a dream, please wake me up from the this nightmare that I did not finish the book I anticipated in 2017.<br/>me : *closes my eyes and pinches my arm*<br/>me : *opens my eyes*<br/>me : well, fuck. this isn't a dream.</b><br/><br/><b>*sighs*</b> I am so disappointed right now. The book that I anticipated and had high expecations failed me. I am not a fan of superheroes, ( I'm more of a p</span>
  <span id="freeText950552607947905086" style="display:none"><b>DNF @ 280 <br><s>REVIEW TO COME TOMORROW.</s></b><br><br><b> THE REVIEW IS POSTED </b> <br><br><b>
  <blockquote>
    <pre><br>She would not fail. And she would not <br>let fear choose her path.<br></pre>
  </blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>me : if this is a dream, please wake me up from the this nightmare that I did not finish the book I anticipated in 2017.<br>me : *closes my eyes and pinches my arm*<br>me : *opens my eyes*<br>me : well, fuck. this isn't a dream.</b><br><br><b>*sighs*</b> I am so disappointed right now. The book that I anticipated and had high expecations failed me. I am not a fan of superheroes, ( I'm more of a person who loves watching wizards or witches or magical creatures ) but I like watching them and few months ago, I watched Wonder Woman at the cinema and I enjoyed it so much. God, the movie was brilliant. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511882953ra/24552147.gif" width="350" height="170" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Before I tell you more about why I did not finish this book, I would like to tell you all that maybe it's just me ? or maybe the book is boring but this kind of thing also happened to me with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1577339523?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Six of Crows,</a> I finished that book but that book was just fine to me, like nothing was spectaculer or something. So maybe Bardugo's books are just not my cup of tea. Maybe. <br><br><b>
  <u>The Reasons I Did Not Finish It</u>
</b><br><br><b>
  <u>The Plot</u>
</b><br><br>I read this book for 18 days and I did not even finish it. Every time, I tried reading it I always got distracted or I fell asleep or I just had to sleep but most of the time, it's because I fell asleep. look, I had never done that since ... I don't exactly know when but it's a pretty long time ago! <br><br>The plot was so freaking boring and I just could not connect with it. The first day I read it, I was so excited and I had these so high expectations towards the book and the more I read it, the more I realized that the book was not like what I expected, not like what I thought and not like what I hoped for. <br><br>Before I read the book, I thought it would left me like this : <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511879680ra/24551748.gif" width="350" height="170" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>or at least, enjoyed the book but I feel like this instead :<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1511879807ra/24551769.gif" width="280" height="170" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>that gif is representing my feeling right now. I am indeed still in shock. In shock of how bad this book turned out to be. In shock that I <b>did not</b> finish the book I anticipated for <b>freaking months. </b> I still remembered how I talked to my best friend about this book, how impatient I was to get my hands on it, how excited I was when I finally got the book. But then it failed me. So just imagine how shocked I am right now. <br><br>I am the kind of person who sleeps late at night because most of the time, I don't really feel sleepy ( because I already nap in the afternoon ) and maybe this book can help me to fall asleep! because that what happened most of the time while I read this book. One moment I was reading it and in the next moment, I was already asleep. <br><br><u>
  <b>Diana</b>
</u><br><br>I swear, Diana was so freaking boring. I could not connected with her. She was so plain and boring and I'm so sure that if Nim were not in this book, I would already abandon this book since weeks ago. Nim is one of the characters in this book and OH MY GOD, she's really awesome and funny. If only she were real, I would be so happy to have a friend like her! Nim is so precious! <br><br>oh and Alia, she's also funny and the way she thought, it was quite funny, sometimes. However, I prefer Nim than her, if I got to choose between them to become my friend in real life. I'm not saying that I don't like Alia. I like Alia but I like Nim more. she's just so awesome! But I still could not continue reading the book, even though I liked Nim. <br><br><b>In conclusion, I might don't like this book but keep in mind that if you want to read this book, go ahead, read the book. Do not let my review stop you because maybe you will like it, who knows, right?</b><br><b>
  <i><br>"Sisters in battle, I am shield and blade to you. As I breathe, <br>your enemies will know no sanctuary. While I live, your cause<br>is mine."</i>
</b> <br><br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br><s>
  <b> I'm currently reading it! Sometimes, I still can't believe the fact that I'm reading it now after waiting and wanting this book for months </b>
</s></span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelby *trains flying monkeys*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelby *trains flying monkeys*" href="/user/show/1053760-shelby-trains-flying-monkeys">Shelby *trains flying monkeys*</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer4107647094561251277"><b>"Because the whole world loves to tell us what we can't do, that we aren't good enough. The people in your own house should be on your side. It's the people who never learn the word <i>impossible</i> who make history, because they're the ones who keep trying.</b><br/><br/>I can't even with how much I loved this book. <br/><br/>It's a different spin on the Wonder Woman story and it's honestly one of my favorites. Diana doesn't find a man on the beach and get all googly eyed over a dude. She rescues a female..AND IT BEGINS!<br/><br/> <b>Sis</b></span>
  <span id="freeText4107647094561251277" style="display:none"><b>"Because the whole world loves to tell us what we can't do, that we aren't good enough. The people in your own house should be on your side. It's the people who never learn the word <i>impossible</i> who make history, because they're the ones who keep trying.</b><br><br>I can't even with how much I loved this book. <br><br>It's a different spin on the Wonder Woman story and it's honestly one of my favorites. Diana doesn't find a man on the beach and get all googly eyed over a dude. She rescues a female..AND IT BEGINS!<br><br> <b>Sister in battle, I am shield and blade to you. As I breathe, your enemies will know no sanctuary, While I live, your cause is mine..</b><br><br>This book shows that women don't have to have a boyfriend to make an amazing book. These women are strong and it makes me wonder...WHY THE HECK IS THIS BOOK NOT SELLING ALL THE COPIES? This is what I want in not just young adult. I want this ALL the time.<br><br><a href="https://lunapic.com" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1511220227i/24493427._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I loved every single second in the reading of this book and I wish I still had my Wonder Woman Under-Roos (and that they fit)...because I would have those suckers on and I would be beating off the bad-guys!<br><br><br>ALL THE STARS!<br><br><i>Booksource: I received a copy of the book from the publisher in exchange for review.</i></span>

<div id="review_2075977245" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2075977245" />
    <a title="Deborah Obida" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida"><img alt="Deborah Obida" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604679377p2/54790180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2075977245?book_show_action=true">Sep 04, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Deborah Obida" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Deborah Obida" href="/user/show/54790180-deborah-obida">Deborah Obida</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54790180-deborah-obida?shelf=comics">comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2075977245" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15394481283836552324">I’ve always being a fan of wonder woman, the idea of a strong female not a damsel in distress appeals to my feminism. I’ve read comic books about wonder woman, watched animations and the movie and I love them all, when I found out about this book and that Leigh was going to write I just could not contain my excitement.<br/><br/>This book is everything I thought it'll be and more. The world building is so explicit and the setting perfectly depicted, I have a perfect picture of Themyscira and the Amazons in</span>
  <span id="freeText15394481283836552324" style="display:none">I’ve always being a fan of wonder woman, the idea of a strong female not a damsel in distress appeals to my feminism. I’ve read comic books about wonder woman, watched animations and the movie and I love them all, when I found out about this book and that Leigh was going to write I just could not contain my excitement.<br /><br />This book is everything I thought it'll be and more. The world building is so explicit and the setting perfectly depicted, I have a perfect picture of Themyscira and the Amazons in my head. I love the plot, despite this been a retelling there is still a lot of originality in this, Teenage wonder woman and a co female protagonist, what could be more perfect than that. Things about Diana like how she felt out of place among the Amazons cause she is not a warrior like them and her desperation to prove herself is all in this book.<br /><br /><b>
  <i> Alia nodded, and Diana placed her fist over her heart. “Sister in battle, I am shield and blade to you. As I breathe, your enemies will know no sanctuary. While I live, your cause is mine.” </i>
</b><br /><br />I love the characters in this book, their banter and crazy conversations, trust Leigh to incorporate that when their lives are in danger.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“That’s perfect,” said Theo, sitting up.<br />Jason crossed his arms. “How’s that exactly?”<br />“We’re the villains! It’s always cooler to be the villain. You get to wear black and have a lair and brood. Besides, girls can’t resist a bad boy.”<br />“You are such an idiot,” said Nim. </i>
</b><br /><br />I really love this car part.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>“Wait a minute,” said Jason. “Can any of us even drive?”<br />“I drove,” said Theo. “Once.”<br />“That was a golf cart,” said Alia.<br />“So? It had four wheels and went vroom.”<br />“You crashed it into a tree.”<br />“I’ll have you know that tree had been drinking.”<br />“Everybody, relax,” said Nim. “I can drive.” </i>
</b><br /><br /><b>Plot</b><br />Diana rescued a girl from the river and a few hours later, sickness like a plague broke out and Amazons that have never been sick fell sick, afterward earthquakes followed. Diana sort out the Oracle to find out whether it was the girl she saved and stashed in a cave on the Island that is causing everything.<br /><br />The Oracle told her that the girl is a Warbringer and a descendent of Helen of Troy (apparently it wasn’t just her beauty that caused the war, she just tend to bring war and discourse wherever she goes). The Oracle gave her three options either the girl die, Diana do nothing or Diana saved the girl and stop the curse from ever passing on to someone else.<br /><br />Diana decided to help Alia the Warbringer break the curse, more to prove herself than it being about Alia. They both set out to Greece but the magical teleportation thingy took them to NY instead all because Alia wanted to go home. They met Jason, Alia's control freak of an elder brother. Alia was still in denial of her being a warbringer till her brother clarified that it is true and their parents were aware. He agreed to help them get to Greece if only Alia attends their fundraiser gala<s>Their parents had a multi-million dollar foundation before they died, now Jason is kind of in charge</s>.<br /><br />They were attacked by some assassins that are aware of what a warbringer can do, they want to kill Alia to end the war but Diana saved the day<s> that scene was so cool!</s>. They escaped and went to Greece with lots of difficulties. They manage to get to the spring that was when shit went to hell.<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Eris and other gods that profit from war tried to stop them not to mention Jason, Alia’s brother is the villain and he don’t want her to break the curse, cause he is already using their blood to make super soliders and if a war starts they will make lots of money from selling the serum<s>Jason has super powers, specifically super strength</s> . He had the soldiers kill Nim and Theo their friends that went along with them, but they were brought back to life by the gods due to the bargain Diana made with them. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />As expected Diana saved the day and went back to themyscira.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15394481283836552324" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2047234383" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2047234383" />
    <a title="Nicole" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/40997852-nicole"><img alt="Nicole" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605132719p2/40997852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2047234383?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nicole" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nicole" href="/user/show/40997852-nicole">Nicole</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40997852-nicole?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40997852-nicole?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/40997852-nicole?shelf=ya">ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2047234383" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9232788513540944425">Before I start this review, I think you might want to know 2 things:<br/>1) I’ve only ever read Shadow and Bone by Leigh Bardugo. It was fun but nothing impressive.<br/>2) I’m not a DC fan. Not that I hate it, but rather that I don’t know much about it. I haven’t read any of the comics and I’ve only watched a movie or 2. So my knowledge about Wonder Woman is very limited. <br/>That’s why I won’t compare this book to any of Bardugo’s other works. I can’t tell you if this book is good or bad compared to her othe</span>
  <span id="freeText9232788513540944425" style="display:none">Before I start this review, I think you might want to know 2 things:<br />1) I’ve only ever read Shadow and Bone by Leigh Bardugo. It was fun but nothing impressive.<br />2) I’m not a DC fan. Not that I hate it, but rather that I don’t know much about it. I haven’t read any of the comics and I’ve only watched a movie or 2. So my knowledge about Wonder Woman is very limited. <br />That’s why I won’t compare this book to any of Bardugo’s other works. I can’t tell you if this book is good or bad compared to her other work. I can’t tell you if WW:W is faithful to the original story or if it’s a good superhero story. However, what I can tell you is whether or not this story was a good read, just by evaluating this book as I would any other, regardless of who the author or the MC is. For those who don't know much about this superhero, don't worry, you won't feel confused or anything.<br /> <br />OK. Let’s start!<br /> <br />Wonder Woman: Warbringer was on everyone’s most anticipated books list for 2017. I was looking forward to reading it because, maybe, it’ll make me want to watch DC related movies and works. The good news is I’m definitely going to watch some… but that’s only because of my friends and certainly not this book. Was it a disappointment? Oh, yes.<br /> <br /><u>
  <b>Summary:</b>
</u><br />When Diana saves a girl from a drowning ship, she soon discovers that this girl, Alia, is a Warbringer. If her sisters were to discover what she had done, she would probably be exiled. Wanting to prove herself as a true Amazon and refusing to leave Alia to die, Diana leaves the island to take Alia to Helen’s tomb in Greece to be purified and, thus, prevent an upcoming war.<br /> <br /><u>
  <b>The Characters:</b>
</u><br />I’ll start with the characters because they were my main problem.<br />It’s always easier to get attached to a book when you connect with the character, and I liked Diana quite a lot. She always tries to do her best. She’s ready to make sacrifices for others and she’s badass. She also seems quite fascinated with the mortal world, her remarks were funny. I wish the book was more focused on her but I think that's why we have Warbringer in the title. <br /><br /><br />Anddd… that’s it. She’s the only character I could stand in this book.<br /> <br /><b>✘ Alia: </b>She’s okay. The story is told from her pov (3rd person) and Diana's. She tried to be her best self after discovering so suddenly what she is. However, while I didn’t hate her, I didn’t like her much, either. Not my kind of MC. I just couldn’t relate to her. Sometimes nothing is wrong with a character, but you simply can’t feel a bond. There was some character development by the end, and I did finish the book with a slightly higher opinion of her. Still, I didn’t sympathize with Alia much and even though the point of this book is female friendship - something I admire Leigh for doing here - it didn’t feel natural at all to me. I think it might be because I liked one of the two girls a lot, while the other as “meh”.<br /> <br /><b>✘ Jason:</b> I don’t like the name Jason. I hate it. Many here might relate to this, to having a name you just can’t stand; maybe it reminds you of some you dislike or maybe you just don’t like it… for whatever reason. So you might say I was prejudiced against this character from the start, just from the name. But the more I read about him and saw what he did, the less of a fan I became. He is so rigid, so dull, and so controlling. He is just so annoying. No, you should not do that. No, you should not say that. No, no, no. Everything about him is a “no”. Nothing was interesting about him.<br /> <br /><b>✘ Theo and Nim:</b> Like Alia, I wouldn’t say I hate them, but I’m not a fan either. But I would say I like them the best after Diana. Still, they aren’t anything memorable. They aren’t funny, either. Their sense of humor is silly and ridiculous. Also, what’s with jokes in dangerous situations? It’s so not cool. Get serious, would you! <br /> <br /><b>✘ The Amazon Sisters:</b> They played an interesting part in the first few chapters of the book. This made me want to know more about these kickass women. Sadly, my curiosity wasn’t satisfied, as Diana spent very little time with them, and later left the island.<br /> <br /><u>
  <b>The Story:</b>
</u><br />In some books, even when you don’t care much about the characters, the plot itself is sometimes gripping enough that you can’t stop reading. Wonder Woman: Warbringer isn’t one of these. I didn’t enjoy the story and was bored most of the time. I couldn’t care about what happened next. I forced myself to continue reading even during action scenes. Things got a bit better after “the plot twist”, which was poor, in my opinion (chapter 25 out of 33). However, I lost interest and had to push myself to finish it. The book was trying so hard to look badass, but it was just really boring. Again, <i>my opinion</i>. It felt like a Contemporary with a touch of Fantasy. The dialogues were a bit stiff and dry more often than not. Like please give some action and stop talking. <br /> <br />What’s more, this book focused a lot on how the Warbringer is a cause for war. Yes, it was mentioned that it’s only a catalyst, yet what was shown was that it’s more dangerous than the greed of men. The war tension and the dangers of one were somehow lacking. <br /> <br />However, I should say that Leigh Bardugo did a great job describing Themyscira. She successfully showed how magical and beautiful the island is - makes me want to live there, forever!<br /> <br /><u>
  <b>The Romance:</b>
</u><br />I hated the romance between Diana and Jason. She’s so naïve because, obviously, she has never had any interaction with men; so, I don’t blame her. However, their thing made me cringe. The dialogue didn’t feel natural, it felt forced. I just hated it so bad.<br />While I understand that Diana should have some romance - and I’m not against that - I just wish it was with someone that is <i>not</i> Jason. Or maybe a better version of him. Maybe a cooler, more understanding, and a smarter one. But if giving him a better personality is out of the question, then no romance at all would’ve been better. <br /> <br />Alia and Theo’s relationship, on the other hand, was OK. It was acceptable because it was almost non-existent. They make a good match.<br /><br /> <br /><u>
  <b>The Verdict:</b>
</u><br />I did not enjoy reading this book. Apart from Diana, I wasn’t a fan of any of the characters. I was bored most of the time and just wanted to finish the book – which I read in less than a day just to be done with it and not because I couldn’t stop reading. I really wanted to like the story, but, sadly, I couldn’t find anything interesting about it. Obviously, I’m in one of the minority here. Everyone said the story was exciting, which made me feel like I haven’t read the same book. I’m still looking forward to reading Batman, mainly because I like Marie Lu’s novels. While the ending was wrapped up, the book could have a sequel. But I really hope it doesn’t. You might end up liking this book better than I did, so please don’t let my review keep you from reading it. However, don’t expect anything mind-blowing.<br /> <br /><b>
  <i>PS:</i>
</b><i> I’ve only seen the movie trailer, but I can tell you, this book is nothing like it.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="9232788513540944425" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="megs_bookrack" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack"><img alt="megs_bookrack" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532027727p2/48328025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2127756961?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="megs_bookrack" class="user" itemprop="url" name="megs_bookrack" href="/user/show/48328025-megs-bookrack">megs_bookrack</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2127756961" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3833305426750908020"><i>Wonder Woman: Warbringer</i> is a wonderful adventure story!<br/><br/>We follow, Diana, Wonder Woman, as she navigates a journey of self-discovery from the isolated island of the Amazons to modern day New York City and Greece. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551979045ra/27169016.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Along the way she learns a lot about herself, life, friendship, love, loyalty and ass-kicking. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551979045ra/27169017.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I thoroughly enjoyed this book. <br/><br/>I felt it had just the right amount of <b>action, turmoil and humor</b>. This is actually the first book I have ever read by Leigh Bardugo.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551979045ra/27169018.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I know, I know. I have been </span>
  <span id="freeText3833305426750908020" style="display:none"><i>Wonder Woman: Warbringer</i> is a wonderful adventure story!<br><br>We follow, Diana, Wonder Woman, as she navigates a journey of self-discovery from the isolated island of the Amazons to modern day New York City and Greece. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551979045ra/27169016.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Along the way she learns a lot about herself, life, friendship, love, loyalty and ass-kicking. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551979045ra/27169017.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I thoroughly enjoyed this book. <br><br>I felt it had just the right amount of <b>action, turmoil and humor</b>. This is actually the first book I have ever read by Leigh Bardugo.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551979045ra/27169018.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I know, I know. I have been slacking in life. We know this about me.<br><br>Regardless, I was really impressed with her writing style. The flow and pace are spot on for my tastes and I think she did a fabulous job of creating an original story of a well-loved action figure. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1551979045ra/27169019.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I did listen to the audiobook for this one and thought the narration was excellent!<br><br>I definitely plan to check out the rest of the books in the <i>DC Icons</i> series.</span>

  <span id="freeText3679831294288087006" style="display:none">I probably look like a snotty frog right now and I’m honestly okay with it.<br /><br /><br />THIS BOOK IS OUT OF THE WORLD.<br /><br />Here’s the run through:<br />•Diana is the strongest badass supermodel. Also, she’s clueless about this whole human world which is btw THE SMARTEST WAY TO ADD HUMOUR. Pat on the back to you Bardugo <br />haha I just love laughing at characters who are supposedly smart and great and strong immortal yet placed in another world, they instantly become simply a fish on land <br /><br />:)<br /><br />Anyways, besides the whole glory of her legs, I feel you gurl...*sniff* I try to make my momma proud too. So cut the crap about feeling guilty for wanting to be noticed. <br />You, my dear, have become one of your sisters.<br /><br />•Alia, Alia, Alia....honestly, I thought she was so whiny, and blind to everything that’s going on but who can blame her when she had a freaking brute as her brother <s><br />bodyguard? <br /><br />I only wish you had run away as a child. (Jk jk this story wouldn’t happen then) <br /><br />•and heerrreee is the one and only, (a freaking blue eyed boy again) JASON *grits teeth at his unoriginal name*<br /><br />This f*cking pig deserves to be sent to the deepest parts of hell, and live an eternity hearing and seeing all of the horrors of earth that he is just FUCKING OBLIVIOUS TO.<br />JUST STAB HIMSELF WITH HIS OWN SYRINGE OF SUPERNATURAL DEATH.<br />Then he’ll get a taste of his own medicine, the little shit.<br /><br />•Nim....yet again, another friend that I most surely need to meet before I die <br />YOU ROCK YOUR HERITAGE GIRL. YOU ROCK YOUR BODY. YOU ROCK YOUR FUTURE CAREER OF BEING A DESIGNER. <br />XOXO<br /><br />•Theo.<br />You carried a sword for a solid ten seconds...<br />*sniff* your shit of a father might not care for that but I do.<br /><br /><br />Speaking of sword, clap if you believe that Queen Bardugo has brought yet another brilliant war for the ending.<br /><br />_______________________________________________<br />*a moment for silence as I wait for you to end clapping* <br />_______________________________________________<br /><br />When that time came where everyone died just so Bardugo could take a moment to rip out our hearts....<br /><br />I would’ve kicked her ass.<br /><br />because of course, not only is it New York tradition, but killing off basically every character I hold dear to heart is an approach that I thought Bardugo would’ve never taken.<br /><br />Mostly because: EVERY AUTHOR WANTS TO GO THAT WAY. <br />Like, is it just me?? <br />It’s somehow an unspoken rule between the authors: SOMEONE MUST DIE BEFORE YOU END YOUR BOOK.<br /><br />However, never fear, my reader, you fellow fangirl still wholly loved and worshipped the ending because dude...who cannot not like the ending when they see Jason sobbing on the ground? <br />IT’S LEGIT TIME TO SING KUMBAYA.<br /><br /><br />And as the song ends and friends separate *cue sobbing..again*<br />I realized.....<br />Why the hell can’t there be a sequel? <br /><br /><br />I’m sending out a wish to you Bardugo, for my next birthday about 11 months away from now: I’d like you to grant me a second book of Warbringer. <br />Thank you.</s></span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1761422908" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1842326190098313525">This book was marvelous. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1504204643ra/23734162.gif' alt='' width='350' height='175' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Bardugo took a legend and made an empowering, feminist book that will help women come into their own. Like I want to go stand on top of a building and look down at the world. Swing down and punch some misogynist in the face and show them how great women are. <br/><br/>I might be channeling my inner Spiderman with that last comment... wrong comic company. Let’s get back on track.<br/><br/>*puts on the wonder woman costume that I haven’t owned for five years that hasn’t been in the back of my</span>
  <span id="freeText1842326190098313525" style="display:none">This book was marvelous. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1504204643ra/23734162.gif" alt="" width="350" height="175" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Bardugo took a legend and made an empowering, feminist book that will help women come into their own. Like I want to go stand on top of a building and look down at the world. Swing down and punch some misogynist in the face and show them how great women are. <br><br>I might be channeling my inner Spiderman with that last comment... wrong comic company. Let’s get back on track.<br><br>*puts on the wonder woman costume that I haven’t owned for five years that hasn’t been in the back of my closet waiting for a time like this*<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1504204643i/23734163.png" alt="" width="300" height="232" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This poster (that if you submitted your receipt for preordering the book) is beautiful. You can see that the race representation has shifted towards People of Color. People of Color Representation has been something that book readers and movie watchers and people in general have been screaming for, and Bardugo delivered. <br><br>The book even touches on the prejudice still lingering in our country when it comes to skin color. It’s not the focal point, but she does touch on it.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1504204643ra/23734158.gif" alt="" width="350" height="175" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>Characters:</u><br><b>Diana</b>: Our Wonder Woman who never is actually never called Wonder Woman because this is kind of an origins story. Her journey isn’t really the main journey, which has disappointed some people, but I like the idea that we see her from other people’s perspective and then her own. <br><br>And yes,<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1504204703ra/23734170.gif" alt="" width="350" height="136" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She can lift a car over her head.<br><br><b>Alia</b>: This is our Warbringer. Basically, what a Warbringer is, without spoiling how they came to be and what not, is that she makes people angry and sometimes she can help a war happen. She doesn’t know that is what she is until she meets Diana. She doesn’t want to live if she can’t undo being a Warbringer (which is the journey throughout the book is finding out if they can “cure” her in a sense).<br><br><b>Jason</b>: Jason is Alia’s brother. His whole life has been trying to keep Alia safe. He buts heads a lot with Diana and he isn’t sure if he can trust her (because he obviously doesn’t know that she is, like, the most amazing woman ever), but he also can see that she is adamant on protecting his sister.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1504204643ra/23734161.gif" alt="" width="350" height="146" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Nim</b>: I absolutely loved this girl. Alia’s best friend is a plump fashionista who doesn’t know why to keep her mouth shut. She’s also into women, but that doesn’t even become a big deal in the book which I absolutely loved. It was just a part of her and not something hated or glorified. <i>It was a normal thing.</i><br><br><b>Theo</b>: Theo is kind of thrown into this group, and he feels it throughout the book that he needs to contribute more to this entourage. He fights with Nim a lot, but that’s not really their faults. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1504204643ra/23734160.gif" alt="" width="350" height="204" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>There isn’t that much romance in this, for you romantic junkies out there. There is a touch of it here and there, but it isn’t even close to being the focal point. To me, that’s totally fine. I do know that some people must have some romance in order to enjoy a book though.<br><br>But I can tell you there is a huge twist in the end and it makes you give the side eye to everyone you know because <b>NO ONE CAN BE TRUSTED</b>. <br><br>I did feel like the story was a little rushed, and I think that is because Bardugo is used to writing series not standalones. It was still an amazing ride and I cherish this book and can’t wait for Batman! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1504204643ra/23734159.gif" alt="" width="350" height="162" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="1842326190098313525" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_26036250'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26036250-batman-special-1"><img alt="Batman Special #1" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1603551263l/26036250._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('FBOL7H6scOe7ORLy/LHOPNcxNyZ3BE32q60gPeDey90QSMh2x2/cy6lVvve/Q+iWO7z/lDnlYZ2qYwjgsEjOnQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('VbqMxLbMqZk3TSWJ9XPef24y46li908hYEv5AO27iQRR4c9eDw8FtSUhiYy2gfjVgr8rGywWY0phhdHdvS2MRA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer9255682908199716107">Leigh Bardugo is a #1 New York Times bestselling author of fantasy novels and the creator of the Grishaverse (coming soon to Netflix) which spans the Shadow and Bone Trilogy, the Six of Crows Duology, The Language of Thorns, and King of Scars— with more to come. Her short stories can be found in multiple anthologies, including the Best American Science Fiction & Fantasy. Her other works include Wo</span>
  <span id="freeText9255682908199716107" style="display:none">Leigh Bardugo is a #1 New York Times bestselling author of fantasy novels and the creator of the Grishaverse (coming soon to Netflix) which spans the Shadow and Bone Trilogy, the Six of Crows Duology, The Language of Thorns, and King of Scars— with more to come. Her short stories can be found in multiple anthologies, including the Best American Science Fiction &amp; Fantasy. Her other works include Wonder Woman: Warbringer and Ninth House (Goodreads Choice Winner for Best Fantasy 2019) which is being developed for television by Amazon Studios. Leigh was born in Jerusalem, grew up in Southern California, and graduated from Yale University. These days she lives and writes in Los Angeles. For information on new releases and appearances, sign up for her <a href="https://https//leighbardugo.us11.list-manage.com/subscribe?u=160b0462d4826c60dbb8af320&amp;id=ec014907b2" rel="nofollow noopener">newsletter</a>.<br /><br />She would be delighted if you followed her on <a href="http://twitter.com/Lbardugo" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a>, elated if you visited her at <a href="http://leighbardugo.com" rel="nofollow noopener">LeighBardugo.com</a>, and fairly giddy if you liked her selfies on <a href="http://instagram.com/lbardugo/7" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a>. <br /><br /></span>
